Hiring of LCT for inter-island mobilization from Vilufushi to Rasmale

Date: 05th March 2026

1. Introduction 
Jan De Nul invites quotations from eligible and experienced transport service providers for the provision of 1 x LCT for inter-island mobilisation from Vilufushi to Rasmale. 

2. Scope of Operations

 Operational requirements
Operations shall be based on 7 days / 24 hours availability, including entering/exit port
LCTs must allow safe driving off 20ft. container using CAT 980 wheel loader. Minimum ramp & ramp support tower width of 6.5 m
Crew to complete the lashing & sea fastening with supervision of JDN
Job 1
Time charter based (3 days, with possible extension)
LCT specification: earliest availability 
Scope of work: 
Start on 07/02 07:00 AM at Vilufushi
Heavy equipment (2x excavators, 2x bulldozers, 1x wheelloader)
Loading & offloading by JDN
Fuel provided by JDN

WELL LAND INVESTMENT PVT. LTD.  |  ANTRAC HOLDING GROUP
FLEET STATUS & REPAIR REPORT
Prepared by: Ali Mushthaq Ibrahim, GM Logistics  |  Date: 22 April 2026


1. Fleet Overview
This report covers all active equipment deployed across Well Land project sites and the Thilafushi base. Three PC350 excavators at Bodufinolhu and one PC350 at Muthaafushi are currently experiencing active faults. Management approval has been received to proceed with a reconditioned hydraulic pump purchase for one grounded unit.


2. Muthaafushi Resort Development Site
WL-HV-0005 — Kobelco SK380, High Bed  |  Status: Operational
Air filter due for service — can be cleaned and reused. No procurement required.
No operational impact. Schedule cleaning at next maintenance window.

WL-HV-0006 — Komatsu PC350, Low Bed  |  Status: GROUNDED
Active faults:
Pilot block failed — failed after only 4 hours following previous repair. Parts being sourced. Quotation received from Infra Engineers India (IEPL): USD 1,050 CNF Malé (Ref: IEPL-EX-QT-004/26-27, dated 08 Apr 2026). MVR equivalent quote requested.
Solenoid valve ×2 required — 1 nos in hand at site. 1 nos on order. Quoted MVR 7,992 for set.
Hydraulic main filter — replacement dispatched (1 nos).
Hydraulic strainer filter — dispatched to site (1 nos).
Engine oil hose burst (20 Apr 2026) — burst hose sent to Malé workshop for fabrication. 2 nos fabricated. Dispatching via B.Atoll ferry on 22 Apr 2026 → Thulhaadhoo → collected by Idrees → site.

Parts logistics note:
All parts for Muthaafushi routed via B.Atoll ferry service to Thulhaadhoo. Collected by staff Idrees and transported to site. Sites are not directly accessible by ferry.

3. Bodufinolhu Resort Development Site
Three Komatsu PC350 excavators are deployed at this site. IEPL visiting engineer Mr. Venkata is on site. Infra Engineers India (Mr. Hari Pilla) is the service and parts supplier.

WL-HV-0007 — Komatsu PC350, High Bed  |  Status: GROUNDED — Pump Decision Approved
Active faults:
Main hydraulic pump failure — one side of tandem pump failed. Pump disassembled and inspected on site by Mr. Venkata. Pump internals photographed (March 2026).
Pilot block failure — recurring fault.

Decision (verbally approved by Hameed, 22 Apr 2026):
Proceed with purchase of one (1) reconditioned hydraulic pump.
Supplier: Infra Engineers India (Mr. Hari Pilla). Quoted price: USD 6,000. Shipping lead time: approximately 30 days.
New pump explicitly not recommended — aged hydraulic circuit cannot sustain full pump pressure; cascade failure risk on hoses, seals and control valves.
All other repair works on this machine are halted pending pump arrival and installation.

WL-HV-0007b — Komatsu PC350, Low Bed  |  Status: Standby — Parts Ordered
Active faults:
Pilot block failed — failed after 4 hours post-repair. Recurring fault.
Solenoid valve ×2 — required. 1 nos held by Venkata at site (payment outstanding, included in MVR 7,992 quote). 1 nos on order.
Hydraulic line adapter / elbow fitting — no standard part available in Maldives. Sample fabricated at Ex Ceylon Engineering, Malé. Part ready. Dispatching via B.Atoll ferry 22 Apr 2026 → Thulhaadhoo → Idrees → site.

Parts ordered from IEPL (Mr. Hari Pilla):
2× Pilot block — ordered from Infra Engineers India.
2× Solenoid valve — ordered from Infra Engineers India.
Hydraulic line adapter — dispatched today (22 Apr). Venkata to receive, install, and report machine status.

WL-HV-0008 — Komatsu PC350, High Bed #2  |  Status: Reduced Operations
Active faults:
Hydraulic jack line issue — arm and boom cylinder seals worn.
Arm and boom seal kits dispatched approximately 15 Apr 2026. Repair in progress on site.
Machine operational at reduced capacity pending seal replacement completion.

Advisory:
Given the pump failure pattern across this fleet, it is recommended to procure one spare reconditioned pump as buffer stock for Bodufinolhu. This eliminates the 30-day lead time when the next pump failure occurs.

4. Thilafushi Base
WL-HV-0018 — Komatsu PC70-8  |  Status: Issue
Track line damaged — no standard off-shelf part available in Maldives.
Custom fabrication from Teflon material required. Teflon source: check RKL Maldives.
Fabrication in progress.

5. Visiting Engineer & Supplier — IEPL
Mr. Venkata (Infra Engineers India / IEPL) is the deployed field engineer on site at Bodufinolhu.

FOC (Free of Charge) deployment period: 4 April – 13 April 2026.
Billable period: 13 April 2026 onwards at MVR 800 per day.
As of 22 April 2026: 9 days × MVR 800 = MVR 7,200 accrued.
Supplier / parts coordinator: Mr. Hari Pilla, Infra Engineers India Pvt. Ltd. (IEPL), Chennai.

6. Next Steps & Action Summary

--- File: WellLand_GM_Operations_Report.docx ---

WELL LAND INVESTMENT PVT LTD
Part of Antrac Holding Group

OPERATIONAL FUNCTIONS REPORT

Current Role Assessment & Future Staffing Requirements

Prepared by:
Mustarq
General Manager – Logistics
Well Land Investment Pvt Ltd | Malé, Maldives

Date: April 2026

1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
This report provides the owners of Well Land Investment Pvt Ltd with a transparent account of the full scope of operational functions currently being managed by a single individual — the General Manager of Logistics. It further outlines the minimum staffing structure required to sustain and scale these operations as the company grows, particularly in light of the incoming fleet expansion.

At present, the GM – Logistics role has expanded well beyond its original mandate. Due to the absence of dedicated staff in procurement, sales, accounts coordination, fleet maintenance, and inventory management, a single person is effectively functioning as a multi-departmental focal point. This report makes the case for structured staffing to protect operational continuity, reduce risk, and enable the company to grow sustainably.

2. CURRENT ROLE: FUNCTIONS BEING MANAGED
The following functions are currently being carried out by the GM – Logistics. These span across multiple departments that would ordinarily require dedicated personnel in any comparable organisation.

2.1 Logistics Management (Core Role)
As the designated General Manager of Logistics, the primary responsibility is to oversee the movement, positioning, and coordination of equipment, vehicles, vessels, and materials across Well Land's operations in Malé and surrounding islands.
Coordinating dispatch of equipment and cargo via ferry and inter-island transport
Managing packaging, load splitting, and delivery tracking
Ensuring correct receipt of items at project sites
Overseeing LCT vessel operations and related marine logistics
Planning and managing logistics timelines around island geography and transport constraints

2.2 Procurement & Sourcing (Currently No Dedicated Staff)
All procurement activities across the organisation are currently handled by the GM – Logistics. This includes sourcing for heavy equipment, marine vessels, firefighting systems, vehicles, and general operational supplies.
Identifying and verifying exact part numbers and technical specifications from physical components
Researching and identifying suppliers locally (Maldives) and internationally (India, Singapore, UAE, etc.)
Preparing and issuing Requests for Quotation (RFQs) with full technical details
Evaluating and comparing supplier quotations including currency conversions (MVR vs USD)
Coordinating purchases, follow-up communications, and delivery timelines
Managing supplier relationships and correspondence for all categories of procurement
Examples of recent procurement activities include sourcing hydraulic pumps for Komatsu PC350LC-7/PC300LC-7 excavators, oil filters for the 6-tonne lorry, a seawater pump for the LCT vessel, and firefighting pump systems (Davilian DHm/5AM benchmark).

2.3 Fleet & Equipment Maintenance Coordination (Currently No Dedicated Staff)
The GM – Logistics is responsible for managing the maintenance cycle of all company-owned and operated equipment, including heavy construction machinery, vehicles, and marine vessels.
Diagnosing faults and identifying required parts or interventions
Understanding component-level detail (hydraulic systems, SCR systems, pilot blocks, pump assemblies, etc.)
Coordinating with repair technicians locally and overseas
Tracking maintenance schedules and service intervals for the fleet
Managing repair documentation and communicating status updates to management
As new vehicles and equipment are being imported, the maintenance workload will grow significantly. Currently, there is no structured maintenance logging system or dedicated personnel to manage fleet uptime cycles.

2.4 Inventory Management (Currently No Dedicated Staff)
Inventory records across the organisation — including spare parts, consumables, equipment, tools, and materials — are maintained by the GM – Logistics. This includes:
Conducting physical stock checks and reconciling inventory against records
Correcting and updating inventory registers for all categories
Monitoring stock levels and raising replenishment requirements
Managing the allocation of parts and materials to specific equipment or projects
This is a full Supply Chain Management (SCM) function that requires consistent daily attention and is currently managed alongside all other responsibilities.

2.5 Sales & Rental Enquiries (Currently No Dedicated Staff)
Well Land does not currently have a dedicated sales or customer-facing staff member. When rental enquiries are received — for equipment, vehicles, or other company assets — the GM – Logistics attends to these directly.
Receiving and responding to inbound rental and service enquiries
Providing quotations and terms to prospective clients
Coordinating rental arrangements, equipment readiness, and delivery
Following up with clients and managing rental relationships
This sales function, while not the core mandate, is critical to generating revenue and is entirely dependent on one person being available and responsive.

2.6 Accounts Coordination & Payment Follow-up (Currently No Dedicated Staff)
While the Antrac Group Head Office Accounts team handles the formal financial processing, all payment-related coordination with suppliers and external parties is handled by the GM – Logistics. Suppliers contact this role directly for payment status, invoicing, and account updates.
Acting as the focal point for all supplier payment queries and follow-ups
Coordinating with Antrac Head Office Accounts for payment processing
Ensuring invoices are forwarded, tracked, and confirmed
Communicating payment timelines to vendors and resolving discrepancies
In effect, the GM – Logistics acts as an internal accounts liaison, bridging field operations and the head office finance function.
2.7 Documentation & Communication Control
Maintaining a clear paper and digital trail across all functions is a continuous responsibility.
Drafting and managing RFQs, purchase orders, and supplier correspondence
Preparing internal dispatch instructions, status updates, and maintenance reports
Communicating between field operators, technicians, suppliers, and management
Standardising documentation formats for consistency across operations

2.8 Systems Thinking & Operational Improvement
Beyond day-to-day execution, the GM – Logistics continually identifies gaps in processes and works to improve operational systems.
Identifying inefficiencies in the supply chain and logistics workflow
Proposing and building frameworks for better fleet tracking, maintenance logging, and inventory control
Exploring technology-based solutions for improved coordination in island logistics
Operating as a project integrator — connecting technical realities on the ground with management reporting requirements

2.9 Summary of Functions Currently Managed by One Person



3. FUTURE STAFFING REQUIREMENTS
With the planned importation of new vehicles and heavy equipment, the operational load across all of the above functions will increase substantially. The following outlines the minimum staffing structure required to manage Well Land's operations professionally, sustainably, and without single-point-of-failure risk.

3.1 Fleet Maintenance & Operations Team
Maintenance Supervisor (1 Position)
A dedicated Maintenance Supervisor is required to manage the full maintenance cycle of the growing fleet. This person must have hands-on experience with heavy construction equipment and diesel vehicles.
Plan and execute preventive and corrective maintenance for all fleet assets
Maintain service schedules, oil change records, filter replacements, and inspection logs
Coordinate with external repair workshops and technicians
Report fleet status, downtime, and upcoming maintenance needs to management
Manage equipment operators and ensure safe operation standards

Maintenance Supervisor's Assistant / Fleet Log Officer (1 Position)
A dedicated assistant to the Maintenance Supervisor is needed to handle the administrative side of fleet management, freeing the supervisor to focus on technical work.
Update all vehicle and equipment logs daily (mileage, hours, fuel, servicing)
Maintain a digital/physical fleet register with real-time status of each asset
Prepare and submit regular fleet status reports to Head Office
Coordinate with the Maintenance Supervisor on parts requirements and job cards
Maintain warranty records, registration documents, and insurance details for all assets

Equipment Operators (As Required by Fleet Size)
Qualified and licensed operators must be employed to operate each category of heavy equipment safely and efficiently. Operators should be matched to equipment type:
Excavator operators (for Komatsu and similar equipment)
Lorry / heavy vehicle drivers (Class appropriate to vehicle type)
LCT vessel crew / operators for marine assets
Any additional specialised operators for newly imported equipment
The number of operators should be determined based on the final imported fleet count, with at minimum one primary operator and one backup per critical asset.

3.2 Procurement Staff (1 Position)
A dedicated Procurement Officer should be hired to handle all sourcing and purchasing functions currently managed by the GM.
Handle all local and international sourcing for parts, materials, and equipment
Prepare and issue RFQs, evaluate quotations, and raise purchase orders
Maintain an approved supplier list and manage vendor relationships
Track delivery timelines and coordinate with logistics for receipt of goods
Maintain procurement records, contracts, and documentation
This role should ideally have technical knowledge or be willing to learn the specifics of the industry — understanding part numbers, equipment specifications, and supplier markets.

3.3 Accounts & Sales Coordinator (1 Position)
A combined Accounts Coordination and Sales role is recommended as a practical starting point. This person will serve as the internal bridge between field operations, suppliers, clients, and the Antrac Head Office Accounts team.
Receive and respond to all rental and service enquiries professionally
Prepare quotations for equipment rental, transport, and related services
Follow up on leads and maintain client relationships
Receive supplier invoices, match with purchase orders, and forward to HQ Accounts
Track payment status and communicate updates to suppliers
Maintain accounts payable/receivable records on behalf of Well Land and liaise with HQ
Prepare simple financial summaries or reports for management as required

3.4 Inventory / Stores Officer (1 Position)
Given the volume of spare parts, consumables, and materials that flow through the operation, a dedicated Inventory or Stores Officer is required.
Manage the physical stores and warehouse, ensuring items are properly labelled and organised
Maintain an accurate inventory register for all spare parts, tools, and consumables
Conduct regular stock counts and reconcile with records
Process goods-received notes (GRN) for all incoming materials
Raise low-stock alerts and coordinate replenishment with the Procurement Officer

3.5 Proposed Staffing Structure – Summary



4. OPERATIONAL RISK OF CURRENT STRUCTURE
The current single-person operational model poses significant risk to Well Land Investment in the following areas:


5. CONCLUSION & RECOMMENDATION
Well Land Investment Pvt Ltd is currently operating with a lean but unsustainable staffing model. The General Manager – Logistics is single-handedly managing functions that span logistics, procurement, maintenance coordination, inventory, sales, and accounts — a workload that in comparable companies would be distributed across a minimum of 6–8 dedicated roles.

This report is not a complaint — it is an honest operational assessment prepared to enable the owners to make informed decisions. The current situation has allowed the company to operate, but it has done so by relying on a level of personal commitment that cannot be guaranteed indefinitely, and that creates real business risk.

As new equipment is imported and operations scale, the following actions are strongly recommended:

Immediately appoint a Maintenance Supervisor and Fleet Log Officer to manage the growing fleet
Hire a Procurement Officer to handle sourcing and purchasing independently
Appoint an Accounts & Sales Coordinator to attend to client enquiries and supplier payments
Hire an Inventory / Stores Officer to maintain accurate stock records
Determine the number of equipment operators required based on the final imported fleet and ensure each critical asset has an assigned, qualified operator

With this structure in place, the GM – Logistics can shift from reactive, multi-tasking firefighting to strategic oversight — improving operational quality, reducing risk, and enabling Well Land Investment to grow in a controlled and professional manner.

Prepared by: Mustarq  |  GM – Logistics  |  Well Land Investment Pvt Ltd  |  April 2026
# | Function / Department | Key Activities | Normally Requires
1 | Logistics Management | Fleet dispatch, ferry coordination, inter-island logistics | Logistics Coordinator
2 | Procurement & Sourcing | RFQs, supplier sourcing, part identification, quote comparison | Procurement Officer
3 | Fleet & Equipment Maintenance | Fault diagnosis, repair coordination, maintenance scheduling | Maintenance Supervisor + Assistant
4 | Inventory Management (SCM) | Stock checks, inventory reconciliation, replenishment tracking | Inventory / Stores Officer
5 | Sales & Rental Enquiries | Inbound enquiries, quotations, rental coordination | Sales / Client Relations Staff
6 | Accounts Coordination | Supplier payment follow-up, invoice tracking, HQ liaison | Accounts Coordinator
7 | Documentation & Communications | RFQs, dispatch notes, maintenance reports, correspondence | Admin / Documentation Officer
# | Position | Headcount | Primary Functions Covered
1 | GM – Logistics (Current) | 1 (Existing) | Overall operations oversight, senior coordination, strategic planning
2 | Maintenance Supervisor | 1 | Fleet maintenance planning, repair coordination, technical oversight
3 | Fleet Log Officer / Supervisor's Assistant | 1 | Vehicle logs, status reporting to HQ, job card management
4 | Equipment Operators | TBD by fleet | Operation of excavators, lorries, vessels, and imported vehicles
5 | Procurement Officer | 1 | Sourcing, RFQs, supplier management, purchase coordination
6 | Accounts & Sales Coordinator | 1 | Rental enquiries, client quotations, supplier payment coordination, HQ accounts liaison
7 | Inventory / Stores Officer | 1 | Stock management, GRN processing, inventory records, replenishment alerts
 | TOTAL NEW POSITIONS REQUIRED | 6 + Operators | Full departmental coverage across Logistics, Maintenance, Procurement, Sales, Accounts, and Inventory
Risk Area | Description
Single Point of Failure | If the GM is unavailable (illness, leave, or resignation), all 7 operational functions become unattended simultaneously.
Revenue Loss | Missed rental enquiries during busy periods directly result in lost income, as no one else is available to attend to sales.
Fleet Downtime | Without a dedicated maintenance team, equipment breakdowns may not be resolved swiftly, causing project delays and cost overruns.
Procurement Delays | Critical parts may be delayed if the GM is occupied with other urgent tasks, compounding equipment downtime.
Inventory Discrepancies | Without regular dedicated attention, inventory records drift from physical stock, leading to both over-purchasing and stockouts.
Supplier Relationship Risk | Delays in payment follow-up or communication may damage supplier trust, affecting pricing and priority treatment in future orders.
Scalability Limit | As new vehicles are imported and operations expand, the current structure will break down — there is no capacity to absorb additional workload without new staff.

Response; 
Dear Adam,

We are delighted to provide our quote for the upcoming cargo handling operations at Hilton Maldives Amingiri Resort & Spa, detailed below.

Billing will start when the LCT and crane leave Thilafushi to collect the cargo and will run until the crane completes its work and both units return to Thilafushi.

Our rates are:
- LCT Rental: USD 2,595 per day (plus GST)  
- Crane Rental: USD 1,945.52 per day (plus GST)  
- Unloading Operation at Hilton: USD 1,000.00 (plus GST) (performed by Well Land team)  

Any T-jetty charges will be the client's responsibility.

Operational Details:
- The LCT, with crane support, will position at T-jetty, Malé, for loading.  
- Cargo will load onto the LCT at T-jetty, transport to Hilton, and dock there.  
- The crane will operate only after docking at Hilton.  
- No crane use during transport—operations limited to the Hilton site.  

Thank you.  
Best regards,  
Ali Mushthaq (Mushthaq)
General Manager

WELL LAND INVESTMENT PVT LTD  
LOGISTICS DIVISION  
QUOTATION  
HDPE Pipe Transportation – Maniyafaru to Bodufinolhu  
Ref: WLI -LGS-QTN -2026 -EVS-001          Date: 15 April 2026  
 
ADDRESSED TO  
Evosun Maldives Pvt Ltd  
Attn: Mr. Asi m 
GST TIN: 1085085GST501  
Email: asim@evosunmaldives.com  ISSUED BY  
Well Land Investment Pvt Ltd  
Part of Antrac Holding Group  
Malé, Republic of Maldives  
Quote Ref: WLI -LGS-QTN -2026 -EVS-001 
Date: 15 April 2026  
 
1.  Scope of Work  
Well Land Investment Pvt Ltd (Logistics Division) to provide LCT vessel and Komatsu PC70 excavator for the 
transportation of HDPE pipes from Maniyafaru to Bodufinolhu, inclusive of all mobilization and demobilization.  
Phase  Description  
Mobilization  Load Komatsu PC70 excavator at base (Thilafushi). Sail to Maniyafaru for pipe loading operations.  
Loading  Load approx. 200 pcs HDPE pipes (mixed dia. ~63 –250 mm, ~19 ft each) onto LCT using PC70 
excavator at Maniyafaru.  
Transport  Sail with loaded LCT from Maniyafaru to Bodufinolhu.  
Unloading  Unload pipes at Bodufinolhu using PC70 excavator. Stack/place as directed by client representative.  
Demobilization  Return LCT and PC70 excavator from Bodufinolhu to base (Thilafushi). Demobilization charged to 
client.  
 
2.  Cargo Details  
Cargo Type  HDPE Pipes (PE100, black with blue stripe)  
Estimated Qty  ~200 pieces (mixed diameter: 63 mm – 250 mm)  
Pipe Length  Approx. 19 ft (~5.8 m) each  
Est. Total Weight  Approx. 5.0 – 6.0 metric tons  
Load Port  Maniyafaru  
Discharge Port  Bodufinolhu  
3.  Estimated Time Schedule  
Activity  Description  LCT (hrs)  PC70 (hrs)  
Mobilization  Base → Maniyafaru  3.0 1.0 
Loading  At Maniyafaru  3.0 3.0 
Transport  Maniyafaru → 
Bodufinolhu  2.0 – 
Unloading  At Bodufinolhu  3.0 3.0 
Demobilization  Bodufinolhu → Base  4.0 1.0 
TOTAL   15.0 hrs  8.0 hrs  
Note: Times are estimates based on field conditions. Actual duration may vary due to weather, sea state, and site access.  
 
4.  Pricing

of equipment from base (Thilafushi) to Maniyafaru  1,500.00  Trip 1 1,500.00

--- File: WellLand_GM_Operations_Report.pdf ---
 
WELL LAND INVESTMENT PVT LTD  
Part of Antrac Holding Group  
 
OPERATIONAL FUNCTIONS REPORT  
 
Current Role Assessment & Future Staffing Requirements  
 
Prepared by:  
Mustarq  
General Manager – Logistics  
Well Land Investment Pvt Ltd | Malé, Maldives  
 
Date: April 2026  
  
1. EXECUTIVE SUMMARY  
This report provides the owners of Well Land Investment Pvt Ltd with a transparent account of the full scope of 
operational functions currently being managed by a single individual — the General Manager of Logistics. It 
further outlines the minimum staffin g structure required to sustain and scale these operations as the company 
grows, particularly in light of the incoming fleet expansion.  
 
At present, the GM – Logistics role has expanded well beyond its original mandate. Due to the absence of 
dedicated staff in procurement, sales, accounts coordination, fleet maintenance, and inventory management, a 
single person is effectively functioning a s a multi -departmental focal point. This report makes the case for 
structured staffing to protect operational continuity, reduce risk, and enable the company to grow sustainably.  
 
2. CURRENT ROLE: FUNCTIONS BEING MANAGED  
The following functions are currently being carried out by the GM – Logistics. These span across multiple 
departments that would ordinarily require dedicated personnel in any comparable organisation.  
 
2.1 Logistics Management (Core Role)  
As the designated General Manager of Logistics, the primary responsibility is to oversee the movement, 
positioning, and coordination of equipment, vehicles, vessels, and materials across Well Land's operations in 
Malé and surrounding islands.  
• Coordinating dispatch of equipment and cargo via ferry and inter -island transport  
• Managing packaging, load splitting, and delivery tracking  
• Ensuring correct receipt of items at project sites  
• Overseeing LCT vessel operations and related marine logistics  
• Planning and managing logistics timelines around island geography and transport constraints  
 
2.2 Procurement & Sourcing (Currently No Dedicated Staff)  
All procurement activities across the organisation are currently handled by the GM – Logistics. This includes 
sourcing for heavy equipment, marine vessels, firefighting systems, vehicles, and general operational supplies.  
• Identifying and verifying exact part numbers and technical specifications from physical components  
• Researching and identifying suppliers locally (Maldives) and internationally (India, Singapore, UAE, etc.)  
• Preparing and issuing Requests for Quotation (RFQs) with full technical details  
• Evaluating and comparing supplier quotations including currency conversions (MVR vs USD)  
• Coordinating purchases, follow -up communications, and delivery timelines  
• Managing supplier relationships and correspondence for all categories of procurement  
Examples of recent procurement activities include sourcing hydraulic pumps for Komatsu PC350LC -7/PC300LC -7 
excavators, oil filters for the 6 -tonne lorry, a seawater pump for the LCT vessel, and firefighting pump systems 
(Davilian DHm/5AM benchmark).  
 
2.3 Fleet & Equipment Maintenance Coordination (Currently No Dedicated Staff)  
The GM – Logistics is responsible for managing the maintenance cycle of all company -owned and operated 
equipment, including heavy construction machinery, vehicles, and marine vessels.  
• Diagnosing faults and identifying required parts or interventions  
• Understanding component -level detail (hydraulic systems, SCR systems, pilot blocks, pump assemblies, 
etc.) 
• Coordinating with repair technicians locally and overseas  
• Tracking maintenance schedules and service intervals for the fleet  
• Managing repair documentation and communicating status updates to management  
As new vehicles and equipment are being imported, the maintenance workload will grow significantly. Currently, 
there is no structured maintenance logging system or dedicated personnel to manage fleet uptime cycles.  
 
2.4 Inventory Management (Currently No Dedicated Staff)  
Inventory records across the organisation — including spare parts, consumables, equipment, tools, and materials 
— are maintained by the GM – Logistics. This includes:  
• Conducting physical stock checks and reconciling inventory against records  
• Correcting and updating inventory registers for all categories  
• Monitoring stock levels and raising replenishment requirements  
• Managing the allocation of parts and materials to specific equipment or projects  
This is a full Supply Chain Management (SCM) function that requires consistent daily attention and is currently 
managed alongside all other responsibilities.  
 
2.5 Sales & Rental Enquiries (Currently No Dedicated Staff)  
Well Land does not currently have a dedicated sales or customer -facing staff member. When rental enquiries are 
received — for equipment, vehicles, or other company assets — the GM – Logistics attends to these directly.  
• Receiving and responding to inbound rental and service enquiries  
• Providing quotations and terms to prospective clients  
• Coordinating rental arrangements, equipment readiness, and delivery  
• Following up with clients and managing rental relationships  
This sales function, while not the core mandate, is critical to generating revenue and is entirely dependent on one 
person being available and responsive.  
 
2.6 Accounts Coordination & Payment Follow -up (Currently No Dedicated Staff)  
While the Antrac Group Head Office Accounts team handles the formal financial processing, all payment -related 
coordination with suppliers and external parties is handled by the GM – Logistics. Suppliers contact this role 
directly for payment status, invoic ing, and account updates.  
• Acting as the focal point for all supplier payment queries and follow -ups 
• Coordinating with Antrac Head Office Accounts for payment processing  
• Ensuring invoices are forwarded, tracked, and confirmed  
• Communicating payment timelines to vendors and resolving discrepancies  
In effect, the GM – Logistics acts as an internal accounts liaison, bridging field operations and the head office 
finance function.  
2.7 Documentation & Communication Control  
Maintaining a clear paper and digital trail across all functions is a continuous responsibility.  
• Drafting and managing RFQs, purchase orders, and supplier correspondence  
• Preparing internal dispatch instructions, status updates, and maintenance reports
